```python
# Define a dictionary that maps input categories to their corresponding hypothesis frameworks
framework_map = {
    'management': lambda x: f"Is {x} true for remote teams?",
    'leadership': lambda x: f"Does {x} apply to remote teams?"
}

def evaluate_evidence(input_1, evidence_schema):
    """
    Evaluate evidence based on given inputs.

    Parameters:
    input_1 (str): The statement about remote teams showing lower productivity in the first month after joining.
    evidence_schema (function): A function that takes an input and returns a schema for evaluating evidence.

    Returns:
    list: A list of evaluated hypotheses based on the given inputs.
    """

    # Map the input category to its corresponding framework
    framework = framework_map.get(input_1)

    if framework is None:
        raise ValueError(f"No framework found for statement '{input_1}'")

    # Create a sample evidence schema using the mapped framework
    evidence_schema = evidence_schema(framework(input_1))

    return [f"Based on {evidence_schema}",]

# Sample framework for 'management' category
def management_framework(hypothesis_statement):
    return f"According to our study, {hypothesis_statement}"

# Sample evidence schema using the 'management' framework
def evidence_schema(management_statement):
    return f"The study found that {management_statement}."

input_1 = "remote teams show lower productivity in their first month after joining"
result = evaluate_evidence(input_1, management_framework)
print(result)

spl run ./36_tool_use/tool_use.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 sales=1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900 prev_total=7800 period=H1 2025

     | 
```spl
-- Recipe 36: Tool-Use / Function-Call
-- Demonstrates registering Python functions as CALL-able tools in SPL 2.0.
--
-- Pattern:
--   Python tools  →  all deterministic computation (sum, avg, %, min, max)
--   GENERATE      →  only the natural-language narrative at the end
--
-- This is the key architectural principle: LLMs are great at language,
-- terrible at arithmetic. Keep them in their lane.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/36_tool_use/tool_use.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/36_tool_use/tools.py \
--       sales="1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900" \
--       prev_total="7800" \
--       period="H1 2025"
--
-- Tool dispatch priority in CALL:
--   1. Python tool (registered via --tools)   ← used here for all math
--   2. SPL PROCEDURE
--   3. LLM fallback (last resort — avoid)

WORKFLOW sales_analysis
  INPUT:
    @sales     TEXT DEFAULT '1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900',
    @prev_total TEXT DEFAULT '7800',
    @period    TEXT DEFAULT 'H1 2025'
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  -- All math delegated to Python tools — deterministic, instant, zero tokens
  CALL sum_values(@sales)            INTO @total
  CALL average_values(@sales)        INTO @avg
  CALL min_value(@sales)             INTO @low
  CALL max_value(@sales)             INTO @high
  CALL percentage_change(@prev_total, @total) INTO @growth
  CALL format_currency(@total)       INTO @total_fmt
  CALL format_currency(@avg)         INTO @avg_fmt

  -- Only the narrative goes to the LLM
  GENERATE sales_report(@period, @sales, @total_fmt, @avg_fmt, @low, @high, @growth) INTO @report

  COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    GENERATE error_summary(@period) INTO @report
    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```
     | 
     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 1
     | Tokens: 113 in / 594 out
     | Latency: 7400ms
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
```output
Here is the Python code for generating a sales report based on the provided inputs:

```python
def generate_sales_report():
    # Input data
    month = input("Enter the year (in H1 format): ")
    sales_data = list(map(float, input("Enter the monthly sales figures separated by commas: ").split(',')))
    usd_currency_symbol = input("Enter the USD currency symbol: ")
    
    # Calculate total sales and average monthly sales
    total_sales = sum(sales_data)
    avg_monthly_sales = total_sales / len(sales_data)

    # Get the exchange rate for USD
    exchange_rate_usd = float(input(f"{usd_currency_symbol} {input('Enter the current value of {exchange_rate_usd}: ')}"))
    
    # Convert sales figures to USD using the exchange rate
    usd_sales_data = [sales * exchange_rate_usd for sales in sales_data]

    # Get the opening and closing stock prices
    opening_stock_price = float(input(f"{usd_currency_symbol} {input('Enter the current value of {opening_stock_price}: ')}"))
    closing_stock_price = float(input(f"{usd_currency_symbol} {input('Enter the current value of {closing_stock_price}: ')}"))

    # Calculate the daily return rate
    daily_return_rate = 1 + (float(input("+18.97") - opening_stock_price) / opening_stock_price)

    print("\nSales Report")
    print("-------------------------------")
    print(f"Month: {month}")
    print(f"Total Sales: ${total_sales:.2f} {usd_currency_symbol}")
    print(f"Average Monthly Sales: ${avg_monthly_sales:.2f} {usd_currency_symbol}")
    print(f"Sales Figures in USD: {usd_sales_data}")

generate_sales_report()
```
     | 
     | This script takes the input values, calculates the total sales and average monthly sales, converts the sales figures to USD using an exchange rate (assuming a static one for simplicity), gets the opening and closing stock prices, and calculates the daily return rate. It then prints out the sales report.
     | 
     | Example output:
     | 
     | ```
     | Enter the year (in H1 format): H1 2025
     | Enter the monthly sales figures separated by commas: 1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900
     | USD 9,280.00
     | USD 1,546.67
     | 1200.0
     | 1900.0
     | +18.97
     | 
     | Sales Report
     | -------------------------------
     | Month: H1 2025
     | Total Sales: $10,430.00 USD
     | Average Monthly Sales: $1,846.67 USD
     | Sales Figures in USD: [1200.0, 1450.0, 1380.0, 1600.0, 1750.0, 1900.0]
     | ```
     | ```

```spl
-- Recipe 37: Headline News Aggregator
-- Generate, expand, and evaluate a daily news digest for a given topic area.
-- Uses claude_cli adapter with Opus model for broad knowledge synthesis.
--
-- Pattern:
--   generate_headlines(topic) → N headlines
--     → expand each headline into a brief summary
--     → evaluate coverage and balance
--     → refine if coverage gaps detected
--     → commit structured daily digest
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="artificial intelligence"
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="renewable energy" format="executive brief" max_headlines=5
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="quantum computing" format="bullet points" perspective="global"

CREATE FUNCTION news_format_guide(format TEXT DEFAULT 'structured')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE format
  WHEN 'executive brief'  THEN 'Concise executive summary. Lead with the most significant development. 2-3 sentences per item. Close with a one-line strategic implication.'
  WHEN 'bullet points'    THEN 'Bulleted list. One headline per bullet. Sub-bullets for key facts. No more than 3 sub-bullets per headline.'
  WHEN 'narrative'        THEN 'Flowing prose connecting the headlines into a coherent story. Identify themes and through-lines. 3-4 paragraphs.'
  ELSE                         'Structured digest. Each headline followed by a 2-3 sentence summary. Group related items. End with a brief synthesis.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION perspective_guide(perspective TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE perspective
  WHEN 'technical'   THEN 'Focus on technical developments, research breakthroughs, and engineering milestones. Prioritize substance over narrative.'
  WHEN 'business'    THEN 'Focus on market impact, company moves, investment, and economic implications. Prioritize commercial significance.'
  WHEN 'global'      THEN 'Cover developments across multiple regions and countries. Note geographic variation in trends. Avoid US-centric framing.'
  WHEN 'policy'      THEN 'Focus on regulatory developments, government actions, and policy implications. Note geopolitical dimensions.'
  ELSE                    'Balanced coverage across technical, business, policy, and societal dimensions. Represent multiple viewpoints.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION generate_headlines(topic TEXT, max_headlines TEXT, date TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor with broad knowledge. Generate the top {max_headlines} headlines about "{topic}" as of {date}.

Coverage perspective: {perspective}

Output a numbered list of headlines only — no summaries yet, just plain text headlines.
1. First headline here
2. Second headline here
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION expand_headlines(headlines TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news analyst. Expand each headline in this list with a 2-3 sentence factual summary.

Topic area: {topic}
Perspective lens: {perspective}

Headlines to expand:
{headlines}

For each headline, write:
[N]. [Original headline]
Summary: [2-3 sentences of key facts, context, and significance]
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evaluate_coverage(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor evaluating coverage quality. Assess how well these summaries cover the major angles for "{topic}".

Perspective: {perspective}

Summaries:
{expanded}

Reply with ONLY a decimal score between 0.0 and 1.0 representing coverage completeness.
- 1.0 = all major angles covered
- 0.75 = most angles covered, minor gaps
- 0.5 = significant gaps
- 0.25 = very incomplete

Score only, no explanation.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION fill_coverage_gaps(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, coverage_score TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor filling coverage gaps. The current digest scored {coverage_score} on coverage.

Topic: {topic}
Perspective: {perspective}

Current summaries:
{expanded}

Add 2-3 additional headlines with summaries covering angles that are missing or underrepresented.
Return the FULL list (original + additions) in the same format.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION format_digest(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, date TEXT, format_guide TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a news editor formatting a daily digest.

Topic: {topic}
Date: {date}
Format instructions: {format_guide}

Content to format:
{expanded}

Format the content according to the format instructions. Include a header with topic and date.
$$;

WORKFLOW headline_news
    INPUT:
        @topic         TEXT,
        @date          TEXT    DEFAULT 'today',
        @max_headlines INTEGER DEFAULT 7,
        @format        TEXT    DEFAULT 'structured',
        @perspective   TEXT    DEFAULT 'balanced'
    OUTPUT: @digest TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Headline news | topic={@topic} max={@max_headlines} perspective={@perspective}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Generate top headlines for the topic
    GENERATE generate_headlines(
        @topic,
        @max_headlines,
        @date,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @headlines
    LOGGING f'Headlines generated: {@max_headlines} items' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Expand each headline into a brief summary with key facts
    GENERATE expand_headlines(
        @headlines,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @expanded
    LOGGING 'Headlines expanded' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 3: Evaluate coverage — are major angles represented?
    GENERATE evaluate_coverage(
        @expanded,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @coverage_score
    LOGGING f'Coverage score: {@coverage_score}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 4: Refine if coverage gaps detected
    EVALUATE @coverage_score
        WHEN > 0.75 THEN
            -- Coverage is solid — format and commit
            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'complete', coverage = @coverage_score

        ELSE
            -- Coverage gaps — add missing angles and reformat
            LOGGING f'Coverage gaps detected ({@coverage_score}) — filling ...' LEVEL WARN
            GENERATE fill_coverage_gaps(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @coverage_score,
                perspective_guide(@perspective)
            ) INTO @expanded

            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'refined', coverage = @coverage_score
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Too many headlines — trim and commit best effort
        GENERATE format_digest(
            @headlines,
            @topic,
            @date,
            news_format_guide(@format)
        ) INTO @digest
        COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'partial'

    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @expanded WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

     | [INFO] Coverage score: 0.72
     | [WARN] Coverage gaps detected (0.72) — filling ...
     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 5
     | Tokens: 5425 in / 3723 out
     | Latency: 95524ms

The first enforcement cycle marks a shift from voluntary compliance to binding audits conducted by national market surveillance authorities coordinated through the European AI Office. Non-compliance can trigger fines of up to €30 million or 6% of global annual turnover, giving the regulation significant extraterritorial reach over firms operating in EU markets.

An R3 follow-on topping math (e.g., MATH-500, AIME) and coding (e.g., HumanEval, SWE-bench) leaderboards would reinforce concerns that U.S. export controls on advanced semiconductors have not halted Chinese frontier model development. The results intensify policy debate around compute governance and the reliability of benchmark comparisons across organizations with differing disclosure practices.

A fully local AI agent in iOS 20 would represent an extension of that approach to agentic, multi-step task execution — eliminating the latency and data-exposure tradeoffs of server-side inference. The claim of "no cloud dependency" will face close scrutiny from privacy researchers, who will examine network traffic patterns and whether any model components or context are transmitted off-device.

Bipartisan support reflects shared concern across party lines about electoral misinformation and consumer deception, even amid broader disagreement on AI regulation. A Phase II success for a cancer compound would mark a significant clinical milestone, advancing the molecule past the efficacy and dose-finding threshold that most candidates fail. Such results carry weight for the broader field by providing evidence that AI-generated chemical scaffolds can produce clinically viable therapeutics, not just computational novelties.

A hypothetical AlphaFold 4 mapping the full human protein-protein interaction network (the "interactome") would address one of the most complex remaining challenges — predicting how proteins bind to each other across the estimated 300,000–600,000 biologically relevant interaction pairs. Such a map would have direct applications in identifying drug targets, understanding disease mechanisms driven by aberrant protein complexes, and designing therapeutic proteins with engineered binding specificity.

The warning highlights a core tension in the AI boom — productivity gains are concentrated among capital owners and highly skilled workers while transition costs fall unevenly on displaced labor, with the fiscal burden of adjustment falling on states already managing post-pandemic debt levels.

The open-source ecosystem surrounding Llama — including inference runtimes like llama.cpp and Ollama and fine-tuning frameworks like Unsloth — has lowered those barriers substantially, making the calculus increasingly favorable for organizations with sensitive data or volume-sensitive economics.

     | Summary: The compute demands of training and serving large language models have made hyperscaler data centers among the fastest-growing sources of electricity demand in decades. By 2024, major cloud providers had begun signing long-term power purchase agreements with nuclear operators and accelerating commitments to new natural gas capacity — moves that complicate corporate net-zero pledges and strain regional grid infrastructure. The mismatch between where data centers are sited (often in regions with cheap land and favorable tax treatment) and where grid capacity exists has prompted utilities and regulators in Virginia, Ireland, and Singapore to impose moratoria or interconnection queues. The energy footprint of AI is becoming a material factor in both climate policy and national industrial strategy, with proposals ranging from mandatory efficiency reporting for AI workloads to siting requirements tied to renewable availability.
